# Awesome Patient Trajectory Modeling

A curated, methodology-focused reading list for longitudinal EHR modeling, patient trajectory modeling, and EHR foundation models after 2020.

This list is intentionally strict: it emphasizes reusable methods, model architectures, representation learning, benchmarks, analyses, and foundation-model work over pure task-specific applications.

## What Is Included

- Longitudinal EHR, claims, multi-visit records, and patient journey modeling
- Method papers on architecture, pretraining, representation learning, generative modeling, benchmarks, and analysis
- Foundation-model and LLM papers for clinical timelines, included more inclusively when they contribute new methodology

## What Is Excluded

- Pure downstream prediction papers that mainly apply standard models to one disease or outcome
- Static tabular prediction papers with little longitudinal modeling
- Clinical validation/deployment papers without a reusable methodological contribution

## At A Glance

- Curated papers: 412

### By Category

- Benchmarks and Analysis: 18
- Foundation Models and LLMs: 107
- Generative and World Models: 34
- Method Papers: 51
- Novel Architectures: 83
- Representation Learning and Architectures: 119

### By Year

[2026](#2026) (20) | [2025](#2025) (149) | [2024](#2024) (89) | [2023](#2023) (79) | [2022](#2022) (33) | [2021](#2021) (42)

| [A Multimodal Deep Learning Framework for Predicting ICU Deterioration: Integrating ECG Waveforms with Clinical Data and Clinician Benchmarking](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/b9727d2110319f16f56473aad71820686980b714)    | Foundation Models and LLMs  | Multimodal                    | ICU deterioration and outcome prediction (mortality, organ dysfunction, medication needs, acute deterioration)                          | The authors created MDS ICU, a multimodal deep‑learning framework that fuses ECG waveforms (via S4 encoders) with structured EHR data (via RealMLP) to jointly predict 33 ICU outcomes. Achieving AUROCs up to 0.97 for invasive ventilation, the model outperformed both clinicians and large language models, and providing its predictions as decision support further improved clinician performance. This work demonstrates that integrating heterogeneous ICU data can deliver clinically useful risk stratification and augment critical‑care decision making.                                                                                           | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/b9727d2110319f16f56473aad71820686980b714)                                                                         |
| [EHRWorld: A Patient-Centric Medical World Model for Long-Horizon Clinical Trajectories](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/d94e32a735742968b4b75e96bb669f905e7a98ed)                                                            | Foundation Models and LLMs  | Foundation / LLM              | Simulating long‑horizon disease progression and treatment outcome trajectories for individual patients                                  | EHRWorld introduces a patient‑centric medical world model that leverages a causal sequential training paradigm to simulate future clinical states over extended horizons. Trained on the newly released EHRWorld‑110K EHR dataset, the model outperforms naive LLM baselines, achieving more stable long‑term simulations and improved modeling of clinically sensitive events, underscoring the importance of causally grounded, temporally evolving data for reliable medical world modeling.                                                                                                                                                                 | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/d94e32a735742968b4b75e96bb669f905e7a98ed)                                                                         |
| [NEST: Nested Event Stream Transformer for Sequences of Multisets](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/314d12b0c64bab018f41143f7efdfbfcad9b815e)                                                                                  | Foundation Models and LLMs  | Foundation / LLM              | Representation learning for clinical event streams (sequential multisets of encounters)                                                 | This work proposes NEST, a foundation-model transformer that preserves the hierarchical structure of clinical encounter data by treating each encounter as a multiset of events, thereby avoiding the inefficiencies of flattened token sequences. NEST introduces Masked Set Modeling (MSM), an efficient pretraining objective that improves set‑level representation quality and computational speed. Experiments on real‑world EHR data demonstrate that NEST captures dynamic clinical patterns and outperforms baseline models on downstream predictive tasks.                                                                                            | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/314d12b0c64bab018f41143f7efdfbfcad9b815e)                                                                         |
| [EHR-RAG: Bridging Long-Horizon Structured Electronic Health Records and Large Language Models via Enhanced Retrieval-Augmented Generation](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/a19c40320dee38dcd49a45b67e9b9c2f9a8438fd)         | Foundation Models and LLMs  | Foundation / LLM              | Long-horizon structured Electronic Health Record prediction of clinical outcomes (e.g., mortality, readmission, disease progression)    | EHR‑RAG is a retrieval‑augmented generation pipeline that extends LLMs for clinical prediction on long‑horizon EHR data. It introduces event‑ and time‑aware hybrid retrieval, adaptive iterative query refinement, and dual‑path factual‑plus‑counterfactual evidence reasoning to preserve temporal structure and coverage. Across four longitudinal prediction tasks, EHR‑RAG outperforms strong LLM baselines, achieving an average macro‑F1 increase of 10.76%.                                                                                                                                                                                            | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/a19c40320dee38dcd49a45b67e9b9c2f9a8438fd)                                                                         |
| [Learning Longitudinal Health Representations from EHR and Wearable Data](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/9bd2f0db473c225527c4e9383190752de1d5b89e)                                                                           | Foundation Models and LLMs  | Multimodal                    | Forecasting physiological signals (e.g., heart rate, blood pressure) and clinical risk prediction (e.g., adverse event or outcome risk) | The authors present a multimodal foundation model that jointly embeds EHR and wearable data into a continuous‑time latent representation, trained with self‑supervised and cross‑modal objectives. This shared temporal backbone yields temporally coherent, clinically grounded features that outperform separate EHR or wearable models on forecasting physiological variables and risk prediction tasks, particularly at longer horizons and under missing data.                                                                                                                                                                                             | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/9bd2f0db473c225527c4e9383190752de1d5b89e)                                                                         |
| [One Loss to Rule Them All: Marked Time-to-Event for Structured EHR Foundation Models](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/e6234fbe476901ecc615fa6c2329ecf12e2b92e5)                                                              | Foundation Models and LLMs  | Transformer / Attention       | Predicting time-to-event outcomes (survival analysis) and related downstream clinical predictions such as classification and regression | The authors propose a novel marked time-to-event pretraining objective (ORA) that jointly models event timing and associated numeric measurements for structured EHR data. Compared with conventional next-token prediction, ORA yields more generalisable representations and consistently improves performance across a range of downstream tasks—including classification, regression, and survival analysis—on multiple EHR datasets and model architectures. The study highlights the critical role of incorporating EHR structural information in foundation model pretraining to enhance downstream clinical inference.                                  | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/e6234fbe476901ecc615fa6c2329ecf12e2b92e5)                                                                         |
| [Rethinking Large Language Models For Irregular Time Series Classification In Critical Care](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/4e6b82dbb5b3ce44b0c45a74cf8a8723601d1cc6)                                                        | Foundation Models and LLMs  | Transformer / Attention       | ICU patient outcome classification (e.g., mortality or other critical event prediction)                                                 | The paper systematically evaluates large language model (Transformer‑based) approaches for irregular ICU time‑series classification, focusing on both encoder design and multimodal alignment strategies. It shows that encoders explicitly modeling irregularity provide the most substantial gains, while alignment strategies yield modest improvements. Despite comparable performance to supervised baselines, LLM‑based methods require far longer training and underperform in few‑shot settings, highlighting current limitations in applying LLMs to irregular ICU data.                                                                               | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/4e6b82dbb5b3ce44b0c45a74cf8a8723601d1cc6) | [Code](https://github.com/mHealthUnimelb/LLMTS)                       |
| [TwinWeaver: An LLM-Based Foundation Model Framework for Pan-Cancer Digital Twins](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/2161182a2978bf388f0fd29652ca8c5d37f1221c)                                                                  | Foundation Models and LLMs  | Foundation / LLM              | Predicting oncologic events (survival, progression, therapy switching) and risk stratification for pan-cancer patients                  | TwinWeaver serializes multimodal patient timelines into text to feed large language models, enabling the creation of Genie Digital Twin (GDT) for pan‑cancer event forecasting and risk stratification. GDT lowers forecasting error (MASE) and improves prognostic discrimination (C‑index) over strong baselines and generalizes to out‑of‑distribution trials, while an integrated textual reasoning component offers interpretable clinical decision support.                                                                                                                                                                                               | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/2161182a2978bf388f0fd29652ca8c5d37f1221c)                                                                         |
| [A Multimodal Framework for Prognostic Modelling of Mental Health Treatment and Recovery Trajectories](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/676b4b853e9fe610be6d35104e0ec6eb42c9a93e)                                              | Generative and World Models | Classical Deep Sequence       | Dynamic prognostic modeling of major depressive disorder recovery trajectories (continuous estimation of patient healing over time)     | This study introduces a multimodal framework that operationalizes the prognostic theory of treatment response for major depressive disorder by mapping its core constructs—Patient State Vector, Therapeutic Impulse Function, and Predicted Recovery Trajectory—into concrete computational inputs. It proposes a Time‑Aware LSTM architecture with time‑decay gates to handle asynchronous, irregular sampling, and presents a synthetic validation protocol to benchmark this dynamic model against static baselines, coupled with an XAI blueprint to enhance clinical transparency and ethical governance.                                                 | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/676b4b853e9fe610be6d35104e0ec6eb42c9a93e)                                                                         |
| [A deep state-space analysis framework for cancer patient latent state estimation and classification from EHR time-series data](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/6885210eb5252116d4663c987d7a98ed3b6c8d69)                     | Novel Architectures         | Continuous-time / State-space | Cancer disease progression modeling and severity classification from longitudinal EHR data                                              | The paper introduces a deep state‑space framework based on continuous‑time neural ODEs to estimate and visualize latent disease states from patient EHR time‑series. By clustering these latent states, the authors classify cancer patients by disease severity and uncover key prognostic factors, enabling earlier treatment adjustments and improved long‑term care planning.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/6885210eb5252116d4663c987d7a98ed3b6c8d69)                                                                         |
| [The Patient is not a Moving Document: A World Model Training Paradigm for Longitudinal EHR](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/13f713bb878503406003237504881e0926d26ec8)                                                        | Generative and World Models | Other                         | Disease progression prediction (longitudinal patient state prediction)                                                                  | The paper introduces SMB-Structure, a world model that jointly trains a latent trajectory predictor (JEPA) and a next‑token predictor (SFT) to encode and simulate patient state dynamics from structured EHR. By learning embeddings that capture disease progression without relying on autoregressive token prediction, SMB-Structure achieves competitive performance on diverse downstream tasks across two large oncology and pulmonary embolism cohorts.                                                                                                                                                                                                 | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/13f713bb878503406003237504881e0926d26ec8) | [Code](https://huggingface.co/standardmodelbio/SMB-v1-1.7B-Structure) |
| [Efficient Variance-reduced Estimation from Generative EHR Models: The SCOPE and REACH Estimators](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/59b8af4bd0f5761e702fbb92f585d21cd987acdc)                                                  | Foundation Models and LLMs  | Foundation / LLM              | Hospital mortality prediction (and ICU admission prediction)                                                                            | The authors introduce two unbiased, variance‑reduced estimators—SCOPE and REACH—that directly exploit the next‑token probability distributions of generative EHR models, eliminating the need for expensive Monte Carlo trajectory sampling. They mathematically prove unbiasedness and show REACH consistently lowers estimator variance, achieving up to a ten‑fold inference speed‑up on MIMIC‑IV hospital‑mortality predictions with comparable accuracy and calibration.                                                                                                                                                                                   | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/59b8af4bd0f5761e702fbb92f585d21cd987acdc)                                                                         |
| [AgentEHR: Advancing Autonomous Clinical Decision-Making via Retrospective Summarization](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/d1972db80f51d43ecc222cac9a737dd820558932)                                                           | Foundation Models and LLMs  | Foundation / LLM              | Diagnosis and treatment planning via autonomous EHR navigation                                                                          | This work introduces AgentEHR, a benchmark that challenges agents to perform complex clinical decision-making tasks—such as diagnosis and treatment planning—using long-range, interactive reasoning on raw, high-noise EHR data. It proposes RetroSum, a retrospective summarization framework with an evolving experience strategy that mitigates information loss and keeps reasoning coherent, achieving up to 29.16% performance gains and a 92.3% reduction in interaction errors compared to baselines.                                                                                                                                                  | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/d1972db80f51d43ecc222cac9a737dd820558932)                                                                         |
| [BOBM: an adaptive deep learning framework for extended-window sepsis prediction with cross-institutional generalizability](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/4b40e0858e1470f62cca86fb2077487aca8d8af4)                         | Method Papers               | Other                         | Early sepsis risk prediction over extended (7–28 day) windows                                                                           | This work introduces BOBM, a Bayes‑Optimized Boosting‑Mamba Tabular model that employs a bidirectional optimization learning mechanism in an ensemble framework to predict sepsis onset up to 28 days in advance. The model achieves state‑of‑the‑art AUC scores (0.86–0.95 on MIMIC‑IV and 0.978–0.982 on external data), demonstrating robust cross‑institutional generalizability and providing interpretable insights via SHAP values for clinical decision support.                                                                                                                                                                                        | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/4b40e0858e1470f62cca86fb2077487aca8d8af4)                                                                         |
| [HyDaST: Mortality risk prediction via EHR-hypergraph and dual-scale temporal pattern extraction](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/7364c1065d0d9f83f7cc46e95849403e08f2da35)                                                   | Novel Architectures         | Graph / Hypergraph            | Mortality risk prediction                                                                                                               | HyDaST proposes a hypergraph‑based representation of patient electronic health record (EHR) data together with dual‑scale temporal pattern extraction for in‑hospital mortality prediction. By constructing a patient hypergraph that captures multi‑way relationships among events (diagnoses, procedures, labs, medications) and applying temporal convolution/aggregation at both fine‑ and coarse‑grained time windows, the model learns rich spatiotemporal features that drive risk scoring. Experiments on a large real‑world EHR cohort demonstrate that HyDaST outperforms conventional graph and non‑graph baseline methods for mortality prediction. | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/7364c1065d0d9f83f7cc46e95849403e08f2da35)                                                                         |
| [IKDP: Implicit Knowledge Enhanced Disease Prediction via heterogeneous admission sequence graphs.](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/3ad39a49f8fe04951b197aa23b19d2ce54965ec9)                                                 | Novel Architectures         | Graph / Hypergraph            | Predicting future disease occurrence/readmission from patient admission histories                                                       | The paper presents IKDP, a graph‑based disease‑prediction framework that builds heterogeneous admission‑sequence graphs enriched with implicit medical knowledge. The model uses a graph neural network to learn representations of admissions and related clinical entities, yielding improved disease‑prediction performance over conventional tabular or sequential baselines on EHR data.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/3ad39a49f8fe04951b197aa23b19d2ce54965ec9)                                                                         |
| [Dementia-R1: Reinforced Pretraining and Reasoning from Unstructured Clinical Notes for Real-World Dementia Prognosis](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/24dddc0bbe14efc44bccd2d8ec51c1ee7556dce0)                              | Foundation Models and LLMs  | Foundation / LLM              | Longitudinal dementia prognosis prediction from unstructured clinical notes                                                             | The paper presents Dementia‑R1, a reinforcement‑learning fine‑tuning framework that harnesses a large language model to predict and reason about dementia progression using longitudinal clinical notes. By first pre‑training the model to recover verifiable clinical indices, the approach learns to capture complex, non‑monotonic symptom trajectories before classifying dementia status, achieving an F1 of 77% on real‑world data and matching GPT‑4o on the ADNI benchmark.                                                                                                                                                                            | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/24dddc0bbe14efc44bccd2d8ec51c1ee7556dce0) | [Project](https://anonymous.4open.science/r/dementiar1-CDB5)          |
| [DyGraphTrans: A temporal graph representation learning framework for modeling disease progression from Electronic Health Records](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/54010a4e8d0696f59000b47f9f772d503d93a5e5)                  | Novel Architectures         | Graph / Hypergraph            | Predicting disease progression / forecasting future clinical states in EHR data                                                         | DyGraphTrans introduces a dynamic graph representation framework that captures patients’ longitudinal trajectories as evolving graphs, leveraging transformer‑style temporal encoders to learn disease progression patterns. The model predicts future clinical states or events from EHR data, aiming to improve prognostication while remaining computationally efficient on large‑scale datasets.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/54010a4e8d0696f59000b47f9f772d503d93a5e5)                                                                         |
| [Large language models improve transferability of electronic health record-based predictions across countries and coding systems.](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/d55f9c99804c33a7d2c179312ed3c2c3bc7b970a)                  | Foundation Models and LLMs  | Foundation / LLM              | Mortality risk prediction across diverse clinical settings                                                                              | The study investigates how a large language model can be leveraged to generate more transferable representations of electronic health record data, improving the performance of predictive models when applied across countries and different coding frameworks. By fine‑tuning a pre‑trained LLM on multiplex EHR datasets, the authors demonstrate superior cross‑domain generalization for outcome prediction compared to models trained on local, monolingual data.                                                                                                                                                                                         | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/d55f9c99804c33a7d2c179312ed3c2c3bc7b970a)                                                                         |
| [It Is Time to Move Beyond Task-Specific Critical Care Prediction Models and Prioritize a Foundation Model Built on Continuous Physiological Data.](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/603490f30e4519c31b1acb0d77509e4f09040481) | Foundation Models and LLMs  | Transformer / Attention       | General critical‑care prediction (e.g., mortality, sepsis, ICU length of stay, organ failure prediction)                                | This paper argues that the critical‑care community should abandon many narrow, task‑specific predictive models and instead develop a single foundation model that learns directly from raw continuous physiological data. A transformer‑based encoder is proposed as a foundation, which can be fine‑tuned for diverse downstream predictions such as mortality or sepsis detection. The authors highlight that such an approach would improve reproducibility, reduce duplication of effort, and enable more robust predictions across institutions.                                                                                                           | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/603490f30e4519c31b1acb0d77509e4f09040481)                                                                         |

| [Exploring Scaling Laws for EHR Foundation Models](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/0460ef4c042f24faf9ebc139279af62e4aceb0f7)                                                                                                                                | Foundation Models and LLMs                | Foundation / LLM              | clinical prediction tasks (generic)                                                                                                                                  | The authors investigate scaling laws for large transformer-based EHR foundation models by training across varying sizes and compute budgets on MIMIC‑IV data. They find predictable parabolic FLOP curves and power‑law relationships between compute, model parameters, data size, and clinical performance. These results provide guidance for efficient training strategies and lay groundwork for future powerful EHR foundation models.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/0460ef4c042f24faf9ebc139279af62e4aceb0f7)                                                                   |
| [Cross-Representation Benchmarking in Time-Series Electronic Health Records for Clinical Outcome Prediction](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/67d57b5c3f3b02efadeb02269fe107c72b945af6)                                                                      | Foundation Models and LLMs                | Multimodal                    | ICU mortality & phenotyping prediction; 30‑day readmission & 1‑year pancreatic cancer outcome prediction                                                             | The paper presents a unified benchmarking pipeline that systematically compares EHR representation paradigms—including multivariate time series, event streams, and textual event streams—across ICU and longitudinal care settings. Evaluating a broad set of model families (Transformers, LSTMs, MLPs, Retain, CLMBR, count‑based models, and 8–20 B LLMs), the study finds that event‑stream models consistently deliver the strongest performance, with pre‑trained CLMBR showing superior sample efficiency in few‑shot scenarios. The findings underscore the necessity of context‑specific feature pruning and provide actionable guidance for selecting representations tailored to clinical context and data regimes. | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/67d57b5c3f3b02efadeb02269fe107c72b945af6)                                                                   |
| [Intercept Cancer: Cancer Pre-Screening with Large Scale Healthcare Foundation Models](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/196d14249ca8f448002a62c8766f48895a15d5c5)                                                                                            | Foundation Models and LLMs                | Other                         | Cancer risk prediction (pre‑screening for early cancer detection)                                                                                                    | CATCH‑FM introduces a large‑scale foundation model pretrained on millions of EHR code sequences and fine‑tuned for cancer risk prediction. The model achieves superior performance—50% sensitivity at 99% specificity—outperforming feature‑based tree models and both generic and medical LLMs by up to 20% AUPRC, demonstrating strong robustness across diverse patient populations.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/196d14249ca8f448002a62c8766f48895a15d5c5)                                                                   |
| [Mind the Missing: Variable-Aware Representation Learning for Irregular EHR Time Series using Large Language Models](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/51b155ec55a97fd8d34a0e518b747468985e5877)                                                              | Foundation Models and LLMs                | Foundation / LLM              | Predictive modeling of clinical outcomes from irregularly sampled physiological EHR time series (e.g., mortality, critical event prediction)                         | The paper introduces VITAL, a large language model framework that explicitly accounts for variable types in irregular EHR time series by converting frequent vital signs into a language representation and encoding sporadic laboratory measurements with summary embeddings or a [Not measured] token. VITAL learns temporal context and handles missingness directly, outperforming state‑of‑the‑art irregular‑time‑series models on PhysioNet benchmarks and maintaining performance under high missingness.                                                                                                                                                                                                                | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/51b155ec55a97fd8d34a0e518b747468985e5877)                                                                   |
| [Coefficient of Variation Masking: A Volatility-Aware Strategy for EHR Foundation Models](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/d8158adc0c73b20d372c0c2a383bd67c34f77d1e)                                                                                         | Foundation Models and LLMs                | Transformer / Attention       | Predictive modeling of clinical outcomes (e.g., disease progression, event forecasting) and improved laboratory value reconstruction                                 | The authors propose CV‑Masking, a volatility‑aware masking strategy that assigns higher mask probabilities to highly variable laboratory biomarkers, thereby training a masked autoencoder to learn more informative EHR representations. Compared with uniform random or variance‑based masking, CV‑Masking improves reconstruction accuracy, boosts downstream predictive performance, and accelerates model convergence, demonstrating its effectiveness for volatility‑sensitive foundation model pretraining.                                                                                                                                                                                                              | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/d8158adc0c73b20d372c0c2a383bd67c34f77d1e)                                                                   |
| [Count-Based Approaches Remain Strong: A Benchmark Against Transformer and LLM Pipelines on Structured EHR](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/9131c2d1e51c2584146192748eb419c7002fd27b)                                                                       | Foundation Models and LLMs                | Traditional ML                | Prediction of multiple clinical outcomes (e.g., mortality, readmission, disease events) from structured electronic health record data                                | This study benchmarks three methodological families—count‑based learners (LightGBM and TabPFN), a pretrained sequential transformer (CLMBR), and a mixture‑of‑agents pipeline that turns tabular histories into natural‑language summaries for text classification—across eight clinical outcomes in the EHRSHOT dataset. Across tasks, victories are split between simple count‑based models and the mixture‑of‑agents approach, highlighting that lightweight, interpretable models continue to perform competitively on structured EHR prediction.                                                                                                                                                                           | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/9131c2d1e51c2584146192748eb419c7002fd27b) | [Code](https://github.com/cristea-lab/Structured_EHR_Benchmark) |
| [Deep representation learning for clustering longitudinal survival data from electronic health records](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/387ba8d3b467ff0c982096928fa854deec04e7dc)                                                                           | Generative and World Models               | Other                         | patient subgroup discovery via clustering of longitudinal survival data from EHR                                                                                     | VaDeSC‑EHR is a transformer‑based variational autoencoder that learns latent representations of patients’ longitudinal diagnoses and survival outcomes. By clustering these representations it uncovers clinically and genetically distinct subgroups, outperforming baseline methods on both synthetic and Crohn’s disease datasets, and offering a data‑driven approach for precision medicine.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/387ba8d3b467ff0c982096928fa854deec04e7dc)                                                                   |
| [Leveraging Electronic Health Record Data and Up-to-Date Clinical Guidelines for High-Accuracy Clinical Diabetes Drug and Dosage Recommendation](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/98e53801ca6a60c82f041874aee3bf06b1607d21)                                  | Foundation Models and LLMs                | Foundation / LLM              | Personalized diabetes drug and dosage recommendation                                                                                                                 | The Diabetes Drug Recommendation System (DDRs) fuses EHR, ICD‑10, and drug interaction data with up‑to‑date ADA and Taiwan NHI guidelines via a Bio‑GPT‑powered Retrieval‑Augmented Generation framework to deliver personalized medication and dosage suggestions for diabetes care. The system attains high precision‑recall performance, low drug‑drug interaction rates, and provides explanatory references to applicable guidelines, thereby reducing clinicians’ literature review burden and enhancing decision support.                                                                                                                                                                                                | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/98e53801ca6a60c82f041874aee3bf06b1607d21)                                                                   |
| [Multimodal Foundation Models for Early Disease Detection](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/b30e57a551b6c30172cfa90a18ce539ac0f1118a)                                                                                                                        | Foundation Models and LLMs                | Multimodal                    | Early disease detection across oncology, cardiology, and neurology                                                                                                   | This paper presents a multimodal transformer-based foundation model that integrates heterogeneous clinical data via modality-specific encoders and cross‑modal attention. It combines supervised classification with self‑supervised reconstruction and contrastive alignment to robustly predict early‑stage diseases while handling incomplete inputs. Experimental results show strong predictive performance and interpretable attention maps for precision diagnostics.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/b30e57a551b6c30172cfa90a18ce539ac0f1118a)                                                                   |
| [Multimodal Medical Code Tokenizer](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/0e87337c51dd87d13b69c81f8cd084356f2d1ae7)                                                                                                                                               | Foundation Models and LLMs                | Multimodal                    | outcome prediction, diagnosis classification, drug recommendation, risk stratification                                                                               | The paper introduces MedTok, a multimodal tokenizer that jointly processes the textual descriptions and relational graph structure of medical codes to produce a unified discrete token space. When swapped for standard tokenizers in five different EHR models, MedTok improves AUPRC across several operational and clinical tasks—most notably a 11.32% gain on drug recommendation in the EHRShot dataset. These results underscore the tokenizer’s capacity to enhance foundation models’ representation of complex medical vocabulary.                                                                                                                                                                                   | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/0e87337c51dd87d13b69c81f8cd084356f2d1ae7)                                                                   |
| [R WE ready for reimbursement? A round-up of developments in real-world evidence relating to health technology assessment: part 23](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/d9d751d830dd6edb8513cb023259dfbfaeec3a1d)                                               | Foundation Models and LLMs                | Other                         | disease progression modeling                                                                                                                                         | This paper surveys recent advances in real‑world evidence for health technology assessment, focusing on transportability techniques that allow cross‑jurisdictional evidence to be leveraged when local data are scarce. | [Rethinking Tokenization for Clinical Time Series: When Less is More](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/31e445b504e8efa9131acd8fe7cc060071e56e84)                                                                                                             | Representation Learning and Architectures | Transformer / Attention       | mortality prediction, readmission prediction (plus two additional unspecified prediction tasks)                                                                      | This systematic study evaluates tokenization strategies for clinical time‑series modeling with transformer encoders on MIMIC‑IV, demonstrating that simpler tokenizations and frozen pretrained code embeddings consistently outscore more complex encodings. Ablations across four predictive tasks show that explicit time features contribute little, while value feature importance is task‑dependent; pretrained embeddings dramatically reduce parameters while maintaining performance. The work provides a fair benchmark and guidance for efficient tokenization in clinical AI.                                                                                                                                       | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/31e445b504e8efa9131acd8fe7cc060071e56e84)                                                                   |

| [CSAI: Conditional Self-Attention Imputation for Healthcare Time-series.](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/968c6070a1580c76b95cc1297d884291d59fb6a8)                                                                                | Benchmarks and Analysis                   | Classical Deep Sequence       | Missing data imputation in multivariate electronic health record time‑series                                                                   | The study introduces CSAI, a recurrent neural network that integrates attention‑based hidden‑state initialization, domain‑informed temporal decay, and a non‑uniform masking strategy to perform conditional self‑attention imputation on multivariate EHR time‑series. CSAI outperforms existing imputation methods on four benchmark EHR datasets, improving both data restoration and downstream clinical prediction accuracy, and is implemented within the PyPOTS toolbox.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/968c6070a1580c76b95cc1297d884291d59fb6a8)                                                                |
| [Event Stream GPT: A Data Pre-processing and Modeling Library for Generative, Pre-trained Transformers over Continuous-time Sequences of Complex Events](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/369b23931bd5e25423a3f575604f1d570f490806) | Foundation Models and LLMs                | Foundation / LLM              | Continuous‑time patient event sequence modeling / generation in medical records                                                                | This paper introduces Event Stream GPT, an open‑source library designed to streamline the creation, training, and evaluation of generative transformer models for continuous‑time event sequences in clinical data. It offers a minimal configuration‑based data pipeline, a Hugging Face‑compatible API that handles intra‑event causal dependencies, and standardized evaluation procedures for assessing few‑shot and zero‑shot performance on user‑defined fine‑tuning tasks. The goal is to lower the technical barrier for applying foundation‑model scale GPTs to longitudinal medical event data.                                                                                                                                                       | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/369b23931bd5e25423a3f575604f1d570f490806)                                                                |
| [DKINet: Medication Recommendation via Domain Knowledge Informed Deep Learning](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/ba9528b5d3a5b8d5e05cdb0139c50fcd0ae5c74b)                                                                          | Novel Architectures                       | Graph / Hypergraph            | Medication recommendation for patients with complex health conditions                                                                          | This paper introduces DKINet, a deep learning framework that injects domain knowledge from the Unified Medical Language System (UMLS) into patient representations to improve medication recommendation accuracy. Two key modules are proposed: a knowledge injection module that blends UMLS-derived biomedical concepts with complex clinical manifestations, and a historical medication-aware module that captures longitudinal medication effects. Experimental results on three benchmark EHR datasets demonstrate that DKINet outperforms existing recommendation approaches by a significant margin.                                                                                                                                                    | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/ba9528b5d3a5b8d5e05cdb0139c50fcd0ae5c74b) | [Code](https://github.com/sherry6247/DKINet)                 |

Experiments on established datasets and a newly constructed large‑scale benchmark demonstrate Warpformer’s superiority over state‑of‑the‑art methods.                                                                                                                                                                                | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/9ced9dac3aca804522f474d39595b4c44d277303)                                                                |
| [Synthesize Extremely High-dimensional Longitudinal Electronic Health Records via Hierarchical Autoregressive Language Model](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/42f96cbe5ddefab0f2f984db50d75264e9927a0c)                            | Foundation Models and LLMs                | Foundation / LLM              | Generation of realistic, high‑dimensional synthetic electronic health records for privacy preservation and downstream ML training              | The authors introduce HALO, a hierarchical autoregressive language model that learns the full joint distribution of medical codes, visit sequences, and continuous measurements, enabling the synthesis of high‑fidelity, ultra‑high‑dimensional synthetic EHRs. HALO matches key statistical properties of the real data (e.g., R² > 0.9 for code probabilities) and yields synthetic records that support downstream predictive models with performance comparable to models trained on actual data, while also improving accuracy when combined with real data.                                                                                                                                                                                              | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/42f96cbe5ddefab0f2f984db50d75264e9927a0c)                                                                |

It demonstrates subword information improves semantic representation, whereas global embeddings better support downstream predictive tasks. A CNN‑derived constraint mitigates the sparsity of treatment prediction. Experiments on MIMIC‑III sepsis and respiratory failure cohorts demonstrate that AL‑Transformer surpasses state‑of‑the‑art baselines in forecasting future patient trajectories.                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/1adde2ef77be73960a1118f9f810af5dbfe9393c)                                                                |

Two scalable inference algorithms—particle‑filter‑based and factorized approximations—enable efficient learning and likelihood estimation for the mixture model. Experiments on epidemiological and semi‑synthetic datasets demonstrate that M‑CHMM achieves better data fit, handles missing and noisy measurements more robustly, improves predictive accuracy, and uncovers interpretable patient sub‑groups.                                                                                                                                                                                          | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/e2da9d5432b30f76a8d9c070039cdb626750954e)                                                                |

| [Self-Supervised Representation Learning on Electronic Health Records with Graph Kernel Infomax](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/f5e3cc6e8fccbb7cebbbbb58e2fd6d7339759a2b)                                                                        | Novel Architectures                       | Graph / Hypergraph            | Medication outcome prediction                                                                                                                        | The paper introduces Graph Kernel Infomax, a self‑supervised contrastive learning framework that embeds EHR data into graph representations without altering graph structures. By augmenting node embeddings into two distinct manifold views through kernel subspace techniques, the method learns node‑ and graph‑level representations that outperform existing baselines on several downstream medication prediction tasks. The approach demonstrates strong theoretical justification for graph‑based self‑supervision and empirical superiority on standard EHR benchmarks.                | [Paper](https://www.semanticscholar.org/paper/f5e3cc6e8fccbb7cebbbbb58e2fd6d7339759a2b)                                                   |

The resulting patient representations are fed into simple logistic regression classifiers to predict multiple inpatient outcomes, yielding superior in‑distribution and out‑of‑distribution performance compared to baseline count‑based models, especially over temporal shifts. By leveraging attention mechanisms, the model both improves predictive performance over prior deep learning and machine‑learning baselines and provides interpretable attention maps highlighting key contributing features.
